Alternatively, we can try to compute the equation of circle (BEF) and show that the line through H with direction v is tangent. That is a computational approach. Let's do that systematically.

Set up coordinate system as before: M=(0,0), N=(d,0). Let r, R given with r<R. Let A=(h,k) with h^2+k^2=r^2, (h-d)^2+k^2=R^2. Then B=(h,-k). C=(-r,0), D=(d+R,0). P=(p_x, p_y) with p_x = (d+R-r)/2, p_y = -(d+R-r)(h+r)/(2k). Note that k>0.

Then k v_y = (╬ö/(2d)) * ( -T (R+r)(d+R-r)/(2d) ) = - (╬ö T (R+r)(d+R-r))/(4d^2). So A┬Ęv = (1/(4d^2))[ (R-r)(d+R+r)(d^2+r^2-R^2) - ╬ö T (R+r)(d+R-r) ].

Now note that ╬ö T = sqrt( (R^2 - (d-r)^2)((d+r)^2 - R^2) ) * sqrt( ((d+r)^2 - R^2)/(R^2 - (d-r)^2) ) = sqrt( ((d+r)^2 - R^2)^2 ) = (d+r)^2 - R^2. Because both factors are positive. So ╬ö T = (d+r)^2 - R^2. That's a nice simplification. So then:

A┬Ęv = (1/(4d^2))[ (R-r)(d+R+r)(d^2+r^2-R^2) - ((d+r)^2 - R^2) (R+r)(d+R-r) ].

Now simplify the second term: ((d+r)^2 - R^2) = (d+r-R)(d+r+R). So second term = (d+r-R)(d+r+R) (R+r)(d+R-r). That is (d+r-R)(d+r+R)(R+r)(d+R-r). So A┬Ęv = (1/(4d^2))[ (R-r)(d+R+r)(d^2+r^2-R^2) - (d+r-R)(d+r+R)(R+r)(d+R-r) ].

Now note that d^2+r^2-R^2 = (d^2+r^2-R^2). Also, (d+r+R) and (d+R+r) are same? Actually d+r+R = d+R+r. So they are same. So let S = d+R+r. Also, let T = d+r-R? Not sure.

We have (R-r)(d+R+r) = (R-r)S. And (d+r-R)(d+r+R) = (d+r-R)S. So the expression becomes:

A┬Ęv = (1/(4d^2))[ (R-r)S (d^2+r^2-R^2) - (d+r-R)S (R+r)(d+R-r) ] = (S/(4d^2))[ (R-r)(d^2+r^2-R^2) - (d+r-R)(R+r)(d+R-r) ].

Now compute (d+r-R)(R+r)(d+R-r). Note that (d+r-R)(R+r) = (d+r-R)(R+r). And (d+R-r) is similar? Let's try to expand or see if it simplifies with (R-r)(d^2+r^2-R^2). We can try to factor something. Let's compute both terms:

Term1 = (R-r)(d^2+r^2-R^2) = (R-r)d^2 + (R-r)r^2 - (R-r)R^2 = (R-r)d^2 + (R-r)r^2 - R^2(R-r). Expand: (R-r)d^2 + r^2R - r^3 - R^3 + R^2 r = (R-r)d^2 + r^2R - r^3 - R^3 + rR^2. Combine like terms: r^2R + rR^2 = rR(r+R) = rR(r+R). So Term1 = (R-r)d^2 + rR(r+R) - r^3 - R^3. But R^3 + r^3 = (R+r)(R^2 - Rr + r^2). So Term1 = (R-r)d^2 + rR(r+R) - (R+r)(R^2 - Rr + r^2) = (R-r)d^2 + rR(r+R) - (R+r)(R^2 - Rr + r^2). Factor (R+r): rR(r+R) = (R+r) rR. So Term1 = (R-r)d^2 + (R+r)rR - (R+r)(R^2 - Rr + r^2) = (R-r)d^2 + (R+r)[rR - (R^2 - Rr + r^2)] = (R-r)d^2 + (R+r)[rR - R^2 + Rr - r^2] = (R-r)d^2 + (R+r)[2Rr - R^2 - r^2] = (R-r)d^2 + (R+r)[-(R^2 -2Rr + r^2)] = (R-r)d^2 - (R+r)(R-r)^2 = (R-r)[d^2 - (R+r)(R-r)] = (R-r)[d^2 - (R^2 - r^2)]. Now Term2 = (d+r-R)(R+r)(d+R-r) = (d+r-R)(R+r)(d+R-r). Note that (d+r-R) and (d+R-r) are symmetric? Let's compute product: (d+r-R)(d+R-r) = (d + (r-R))(d + (R-r)) = (d + (r-R))(d - (r-R))? Now bracket = Term1 - Term2 = (R-r)(d^2 - (R^2 - r^2)) - (R+r)(d^2 - (R-r)^2). Expand: (R-r)d^2 - (R-r)(R^2 - r^2) - (R+r)d^2 + (R+r)(R-r)^2. Combine d^2 terms: [(R-r) - (R+r)]d^2 = (-2r)d^2. So bracket = -2r d^2 - (R-r)(R^2 - r^2) + (R+r)(R-r)^2.

LetŌĆÖs denote coordinates: B=(9/10, -3ŌłÜ91/10). E=(109/46, -7ŌłÜ91/46). F=(2311/690, -313ŌłÜ91/690). We can find O by solving the linear equations from perpendicular bisectors.

We have three points: P1=B, P2=E, P3=F. The circumcenter O=(x,y) satisfies:

(x - x1)^2 + (y - y1)^2 = (x - x2)^2 + (y - y2)^2 = (x - x3)^2 + (y - y3)^2.

From first equality: (x - x1)^2 + (y - y1)^2 = (x - x2)^2 + (y - y2)^2 => expand: x^2 -2x x1 + x1^2 + y^2 -2y y1 + y1^2 = x^2 -2x x2 + x2^2 + y^2 -2y y2 + y2^2 => cancel x^2,y^2: -2x x1 + x1^2 -2y y1 + y1^2 = -2x x2 + x2^2 -2y y2 + y2^2 => bring terms: -2x(x1-x2) -2y(y1-y2) = x2^2+y2^2 - (x1^2+y1^2). So linear equation: 2(x2-x1)x + 2(y2-y1)y = (x2^2+y2^2) - (x1^2+y1^2). Similarly for other pair.

Thus we can compute O.

LetŌĆÖs compute using vectors. LetŌĆÖs define coordinates in a more systematic way. Since all points have y-coordinate proportional to ŌłÜ91, we can write:

B = (b_x, b_y) = (9/10, -3ŌłÜ91/10)
E = (e_x, e_y) = (109/46, -7ŌłÜ91/46)
F = (f_x, f_y) = (2311/690, -313ŌłÜ91/690)

But maybe we can simplify using relation to S? Actually note that F is on ╬ō, so |F-N|^2 = R^2. But we can compute f_x^2+f_y^2? Not directly. Alternatively, we can use the fact that B, E, F are points, and the circumcenter O might have a nice form. Perhaps there is a synthetic relation: The circle (BEF) is the image of the circle with diameter something under some transformation. Given the complexity, maybe we can avoid computing O explicitly by using the condition for tangency in terms of power and distances.

We need to show that the line through H parallel to v is tangent to circle (BEF). That is equivalent to: The distance from O to line L equals radius R_circ. But we can also use the fact that for a line through H, it is tangent to circle (BEF) if and only if the power of H with respect to circle (BEF) equals the square of the distance from H to the point of tangency, but that's not a condition on H alone. However, if we consider the line L, its equation can be written as: (X - H) ├Ś v = 0 (cross product). For a point X on L, we have (X - H) parallel to v. The distance from O to L is |(O - H) ├Ś v|/|v|. So we need to show that |(O - H) ├Ś v|/|v| = R_circ. Equivalently, |(O - H) ├Ś v|^2 = |v|^2 R_circ^2.

But R_circ^2 = |O - B|^2. So we need to show that |(O - H) ├Ś v|^2 = |v|^2 |O - B|^2.

Now note that O is circumcenter of triangle BEF, so we have O - B is perpendicular to EF? Actually O is equidistant from B, E, F. So O is the circumcenter. There are relationships: O - B is perpendicular to the chord? Not exactly, but we can consider the vectors.

Maybe we can find O in a more elegant way. Since E and F are on line AP, and B is symmetric to A across x-axis, perhaps the circumcenter O is the midpoint of the segment joining the projections? Or maybe we can use the fact that the circle (BEF) is the image of the circle with diameter MN? Let's examine numeric for d=5,r=3,R=4: O=(2.5,-2.5) = (d/2, -d/2). That is interesting. For d=5,r=3,R=5: O Ōēł (2.465,-3.020). Not exactly (d/2,-d/2). But maybe O = (d/2, -d/2) is not general. However, note that in the first numeric, we had R=4, r=3, d=5. Let's compute O exactly for general parameters using algebra. We have A=(h,k), B=(h,-k). v = (v_x, v_y) with v_x = ((R-r)S)/(2d), v_y = -T (R+r)(d+R-r)/(2d). And t_E = rS/|v|^2, t_F = RS/|v|^2. Then E = A + (rS/|v|^2)v, F = A + (RS/|v|^2)v.

We need circumcenter O of B,E,F. Let's find O using the formula for circumcenter in terms of vectors. There is known: For three points with coordinates, the circumcenter can be expressed as:

O = (|P2-P3|^2 (P1) + |P3-P1|^2 (P2) + |P1-P2|^2 (P3)) / (|P2-P3|^2 + |P3-P1|^2 + |P1-P2|^2)? That is actually the expression for the circumcenter in terms of barycentric coordinates? I think the formula for the circumcenter in barycentric coordinates relative to triangle is: O = (a^2 (b^2+c^2-a^2) : ...)? Not.

Better: Use linear algebra. The circumcenter O satisfies:

O = ( (x1^2+y1^2)(y2-y3) + (x2^2+y2^2)(y3-y1) + (x3^2+y3^2)(y1-y2) ) / ( 2(x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2) ) ) for x-coordinate. Similarly for y. That formula comes from solving the system of linear equations from the equality of squared distances. So we can use that.

Let points: P1=B=(h,-k), P2=E=(x_E,y_E), P3=F=(x_F,y_F). Then the circumcenter O=(x,y) can be computed as:

x = ( (x1^2+y1^2)(y2-y3) + (x2^2+y2^2)(y3-y1) + (x3^2+y3^2)(y1-y2) ) / ( 2( x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2) ) )
y = ( (x1^2+y1^2)(x3-x2) + (x2^2+y2^2)(x1-x3) + (x3^2+y3^2)(x2-x1) ) / ( 2( x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2) ) )? Actually there is a symmetric formula: The circumcenter (x,y) is given by:

x = ( (x1^2+y1^2)(y2-y3) + (x2^2+y2^2)(y3-y1) + (x3^2+y3^2)(y1-y2) ) / D
y = ( (x1^2+y1^2)(x3-x2) + (x2^2+y2^2)(x1-x3) + (x3^2+y3^2)(x2-x1) ) / D
where D = 2( x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2) ). That's the formula for the circumcenter in terms of coordinates (the intersection of perpendicular bisectors). We'll use that.

Thus we need to compute these expressions. Since we have explicit forms in terms of h,k,d,r,R, and we also have relation between h,k,d,r,R, we can try to simplify.

LetŌĆÖs denote:

x1 = h, y1 = -k
x2 = e_x = h + ╬▒ v_x, y2 = e_y = k + ╬▒ v_y
x3 = f_x = h + ╬▓ v_x, y3 = f_y = k + ╬▓ v_y

where ╬▒ = rS/|v|^2, ╬▓ = RS/|v|^2.

We also have v = (v_x, v_y). And we know that A=(h,k) lies on both circles, so |A|^2 = r^2, |A-N|^2 = R^2.

Now we need to compute D = 2( x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2) ). Since y2-y3 = (k+╬▒v_y) - (k+╬▓v_y) = (╬▒-╬▓)v_y = (rS/|v|^2 - RS/|v|^2) v_y = ((r-R)S/|v|^2) v_y = -((R-r)S/|v|^2) v_y. Similarly, y3-y1 = (k+╬▓v_y) - (-k) = 2k + ╬▓ v_y. y1-y2 = (-k) - (k+╬▒v_y) = -2k - ╬▒ v_y.

Thus D = 2[ h * ( (╬▒-╬▓)v_y ) + (h+╬▒v_x) * (2k+╬▓v_y) + (h+╬▓v_x) * (-2k-╬▒v_y) ].

Simplify inside:

First term: h(╬▒-╬▓)v_y.
Second: (h+╬▒v_x)(2k+╬▓v_y) = h(2k+╬▓v_y) + ╬▒v_x(2k+╬▓v_y) = 2hk + h╬▓v_y + 2╬▒k v_x + ╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y.
Third: (h+╬▓v_x)(-2k-╬▒v_y) = -h(2k+╬▒v_y) - ╬▓v_x(2k+╬▒v_y) = -2hk - h╬▒v_y - 2╬▓k v_x - ╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y.

Sum second+third: (2hk + h╬▓v_y + 2╬▒k v_x + ╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y) + (-2hk - h╬▒v_y - 2╬▓k v_x - ╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y) = h╬▓v_y - h╬▒v_y + 2╬▒k v_x - 2╬▓k v_x + (╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y - ╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y) = h(╬▓-╬▒)v_y + 2k(╬▒-╬▓)v_x = (╬▓-╬▒)[ h v_y + 2k v_x ].

Now add first term: h(╬▒-╬▓)v_y = -h(╬▓-╬▒)v_y. So total inside = -h(╬▓-╬▒)v_y + (╬▓-╬▒)[ h v_y + 2k v_x ] = (╬▓-╬▒)[ h v_y + 2k v_x - h v_y ] = (╬▓-╬▒)(2k v_x). So inside bracket = (╬▓-╬▒) 2k v_x. Thus D = 2 * ( (╬▓-╬▒) 2k v_x ) = 4k (╬▓-╬▒) v_x.

Since ╬▓-╬▒ = (R-r)S/|v|^2. So D = 4k (R-r)S/|v|^2 v_x.

Now v_x = ((R-r)S)/(2d). So v_x = ((R-r)S)/(2d). Then D = 4k (R-r)S/|v|^2 * ((R-r)S)/(2d) = (4k (R-r)^2 S^2)/(2d |v|^2) = (2k (R-r)^2 S^2)/(d |v|^2).

Now compute numerator for x-coordinate: N_x = (x1^2+y1^2)(y2-y3) + (x2^2+y2^2)(y3-y1) + (x3^2+y3^2)(y1-y2). We have x1^2+y1^2 = h^2+(-k)^2 = h^2+k^2 = r^2. So first term = r^2 * (╬▒-╬▓)v_y = r^2 (╬▒-╬▓)v_y = -r^2 (╬▓-╬▒)v_y = -r^2 (R-r)S/|v|^2 * v_y.

Now we need x2^2+y2^2 and x3^2+y3^2. Since E = A + ╬▒ v, we have |E|^2 = |A|^2 + 2╬▒ A┬Ęv + ╬▒^2|v|^2 = r^2 + 2╬▒ (A┬Ęv) + ╬▒^2|v|^2. But we already computed A┬Ęv = -r S/2. So |E|^2 = r^2 + 2╬▒ (-rS/2) + ╬▒^2|v|^2 = r^2 - ╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2.

Similarly, |F|^2 = r^2 - ╬▓ r S + ╬▓^2|v|^2.

Now we also need (y3-y1) and (y1-y2). y3-y1 = (k+╬▓v_y) - (-k) = 2k + ╬▓ v_y. y1-y2 = (-k) - (k+╬▒v_y) = -2k - ╬▒ v_y.

Thus N_x = r^2 (╬▒-╬▓)v_y + |E|^2 (2k+╬▓v_y) + |F|^2 (-2k-╬▒v_y).

Now we can plug in expressions. Let's compute N_x step by step. Write:

N_x = r^2 (╬▒-╬▓)v_y + (r^2 - ╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2)(2k+╬▓v_y) + (r^2 - ╬▓ r S + ╬▓^2|v|^2)(-2k-╬▒v_y).

Expand second term: (r^2 - ╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2)(2k+╬▓v_y) = 2k r^2 + 2k(-╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2) + ╬▓v_y r^2 + ╬▓v_y(-╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2) = 2k r^2 - 2k╬▒ r S + 2k╬▒^2|v|^2 + ╬▓ r^2 v_y - ╬▒╬▓ r S v_y + ╬▒^2╬▓ |v|^2 v_y.

Third term: (r^2 - ╬▓ r S + ╬▓^2|v|^2)(-2k-╬▒v_y) = -2k r^2 -2k(-╬▓ r S + ╬▓^2|v|^2) - ╬▒v_y r^2 - ╬▒v_y(-╬▓ r S + ╬▓^2|v|^2) = -2k r^2 + 2k╬▓ r S - 2k╬▓^2|v|^2 - ╬▒ r^2 v_y + ╬▒╬▓ r S v_y - ╬▒╬▓^2 |v|^2 v_y.

Now sum second and third:

- Terms with 2k r^2: 2k r^2 - 2k r^2 = 0.
- Terms with -2k╬▒ r S: -2k╬▒ r S.
- Terms with 2k╬▒^2|v|^2: +2k╬▒^2|v|^2.
- Terms with 2k╬▓ r S: +2k╬▓ r S.
- Terms with -2k╬▓^2|v|^2: -2k╬▓^2|v|^2.
- Terms with ╬▓ r^2 v_y: +╬▓ r^2 v_y.
- Terms with -╬▒╬▓ r S v_y: -╬▒╬▓ r S v_y.
- Terms with ╬▒^2╬▓ |v|^2 v_y: +╬▒^2╬▓ |v|^2 v_y.
- Terms with -╬▒ r^2 v_y: -╬▒ r^2 v_y.
- Terms with +╬▒╬▓ r S v_y: +╬▒╬▓ r S v_y.
- Terms with -╬▒╬▓^2 |v|^2 v_y: -╬▒╬▓^2 |v|^2 v_y.

Now note that the -╬▒╬▓ r S v_y and +╬▒╬▓ r S v_y cancel. So we have:

Sum = -2k╬▒ r S + 2k╬▒^2|v|^2 + 2k╬▓ r S - 2k╬▓^2|v|^2 + ╬▓ r^2 v_y - ╬▒ r^2 v_y + ╬▒^2╬▓ |v|^2 v_y - ╬▒╬▓^2 |v|^2 v_y.

Now add first term: r^2 (╬▒-╬▓)v_y = ╬▒ r^2 v_y - ╬▓ r^2 v_y.

So N_x = (╬▒ r^2 v_y - ╬▓ r^2 v_y) + ( -2k╬▒ r S + 2k╬▒^2|v|^2 + 2k╬▓ r S - 2k╬▓^2|v|^2 + ╬▓ r^2 v_y - ╬▒ r^2 v_y + ╬▒^2╬▓ |v|^2 v_y - ╬▒╬▓^2 |v|^2 v_y ) = combine r^2 v_y terms: ╬▒ r^2 v_y - ╬▓ r^2 v_y + ╬▓ r^2 v_y - ╬▒ r^2 v_y = 0. So those cancel. So N_x = -2k╬▒ r S + 2k╬▒^2|v|^2 + 2k╬▓ r S - 2k╬▓^2|v|^2 + ╬▒^2╬▓ |v|^2 v_y - ╬▒╬▓^2 |v|^2 v_y.

Factor 2k in first four terms: N_x = 2k( -╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2 + ╬▓ r S - ╬▓^2|v|^2 ) + ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y (╬▒ - ╬▓). Because ╬▒^2╬▓ - ╬▒╬▓^2 = ╬▒╬▓(╬▒-╬▓). So N_x = 2k[ (╬▓-╬▒) r S + (╬▒^2|v|^2 - ╬▓^2|v|^2) ] + ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y (╬▒-╬▓). But ╬▒^2|v|^2 - ╬▓^2|v|^2 = (╬▒-╬▓)(╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2. So N_x = 2k[ (╬▓-╬▒) r S + (╬▒-╬▓)(╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 ] + ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y (╬▒-╬▓) = 2k (╬▒-╬▓)[ -r S + (╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 ]? Wait careful:

(╬▓-╬▒) = -(╬▒-╬▓). So (╬▓-╬▒) r S = -(╬▒-╬▓) r S. Then N_x = 2k[ -(╬▒-╬▓) r S + (╬▒-╬▓)(╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 ] + ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y (╬▒-╬▓) = 2k (╬▒-╬▓)[ -r S + (╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 ] + ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y (╬▒-╬▓). So N_x = (╬▒-╬▓)[ 2k( -r S + (╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 ) + ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y ].

Now we know ╬▒ = rS/|v|^2, ╬▓ = RS/|v|^2. Then ╬▒+╬▓ = (R+r)S/|v|^2. So (╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 = (R+r)S. Then -r S + (╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 = -r S + (R+r)S = R S. So that simplifies nicely! So 2k( -r S + (╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 ) = 2k R S. Also, ╬▒╬▓ = (rR S^2)/|v|^4. So ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y = (rR S^2)/|v|^2 * v_y. So N_x = (╬▒-╬▓)[ 2k R S + (rR S^2)/|v|^2 * v_y ].

Now ╬▒-╬▓ = (r-R)S/|v|^2 = -(R-r)S/|v|^2. So N_x = -(R-r)S/|v|^2 * [ 2k R S + (rR S^2)/|v|^2 * v_y ] = -(R-r)S/|v|^2 * S [ 2k R + (rR S)/|v|^2 * v_y ] = -(R-r)S^2/|v|^2 * [ 2k R + (rR S v_y)/|v|^2 ].

Now D = 4k (R-r)^2 S^2/(d |v|^2). So x-coordinate of circumcenter O is:

x_O = N_x / D = [ -(R-r)S^2/|v|^2 * ( 2k R + (rR S v_y)/|v|^2 ) ] / [ 4k (R-r)^2 S^2/(d |v|^2) ] = [ -(R-r)S^2/|v|^2 * (2k R + (rR S v_y)/|v|^2) ] * [ d |v|^2/(4k (R-r)^2 S^2) ] = - (R-r) * d / (4k (R-r)^2) * (2k R + (rR S v_y)/|v|^2) = - d/(4k (R-r)) * (2k R + (rR S v_y)/|v|^2).

Simplify: x_O = - (d/(4k (R-r))) * (2k R + (rR S v_y)/|v|^2) = - (d/(4k (R-r))) * (2k R) - (d/(4k (R-r))) * (rR S v_y)/|v|^2 = - (d * 2k R)/(4k (R-r)) - (d r R S v_y)/(4k (R-r) |v|^2) = - (d R)/(2 (R-r)) - (d r R S v_y)/(4k (R-r) |v|^2).

Now we need to simplify v_y. v_y = p_y - k. But we have an expression for v_y in terms of T: v_y = -T (R+r)(d+R-r)/(2d) = -T (R+r) S/(2d). And we also have |v|^2 = v_x^2+v_y^2. v_x = ((R-r)S)/(2d). So |v|^2 = ((R-r)^2 S^2)/(4d^2) + T^2 (R+r)^2 S^2/(4d^2) = (S^2/(4d^2))[ (R-r)^2 + T^2 (R+r)^2 ].

Given the complexity, maybe there is a more elegant synthetic solution. Let's search for known geometry configurations: Two intersecting circles, line of centers, points C and D on the circles on opposite sides of the centers, then the circumcenter of ACD, and then the orthocenter of triangle PMN, and then a line parallel to AP tangent to circle through B,E,F. I think the standard result: Given two circles, there are two centers of similarity (internal and external) that lie on the line of centers. The spiral similarity that sends one circle to the other (i.e., maps the set of points of one circle to the set of points of the other) has its center at one of these centers of similarity. For two circles, the external center of similarity is the point on the line of centers such that the ratio of distances to the centers equals the ratio of radii. That point is the intersection of the circles' common external tangents. The internal center of similarity is the intersection of common internal tangents. So those points are on the line MN. So the spiral similarity sending ╬® to ╬ō is centered at one of these centers of similarity, not at the intersection points. a1' = 2d r (R-r)

b1' = 2kQ - 2d r T (R+r)

where Q = (R-r)^2 + T^2 (R+r)^2.

We also have T = (h+r)/k. And we have expressions for h and k in terms of d,r,R. Let's compute T in terms of d,r,R.

We have h = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). Then h+r = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d) + r = (d^2+r^2-R^2+2dr)/(2d) = ((d+r)^2 - R^2)/(2d). So h+r = ((d+r)^2-R^2)/(2d). And k^2 = r^2 - h^2 = r^2 - ((d^2+r^2-R^2)^2/(4d^2)). So k = sqrt( ( (2dr)^2 - (d^2+r^2-R^2)^2 )/(4d^2) ) = (1/(2d)) sqrt( (2dr - (d^2+r^2-R^2))(2dr + (d^2+r^2-R^2)) ) = (1/(2d)) sqrt( (R^2 - (d-r)^2)((d+r)^2 - R^2) ). So k = (1/(2d)) sqrt( (R^2 - (d-r)^2)((d+r)^2 - R^2) ). So then T = (h+r)/k = [ ((d+r)^2-R^2)/(2d) ] / [ (1/(2d)) sqrt( (R^2 - (d-r)^2)((d+r)^2 - R^2) ) ] = ((d+r)^2-R^2) / sqrt( (R^2 - (d-r)^2)((d+r)^2 - R^2) ) = sqrt( ((d+r)^2-R^2) / (R^2 - (d-r)^2) ). So T = sqrt( ((d+r)^2-R^2)/(R^2-(d-r)^2) ). Good.

Now also compute U = d+R-r. And S = d+R+r.

Now note that ((d+r)^2-R^2) = (d+r-R)(d+r+R). And R^2-(d-r)^2 = (R-(d-r))(R+(d-r)) = (R-d+r)(R+d-r). So T = sqrt( (d+r-R)(d+r+R) / ((R-d+r)(R+d-r)) ). But d+r-R = (d+R-r)? Actually d+r-R = (d - (R-r)). And R-d+r = (R - d + r). So these are related. Not needed.

Now also compute d^2 - (R+r)S = d^2 - (R+r)(d+R+r) = d^2 - (R+r)d - (R+r)^2 = d^2 - d(R+r) - (R+r)^2. That is negative. Similarly, R d^2 - r(R+r)S = R d^2 - r(R+r)(d+R+r) = R d^2 - r(R+r)d - r(R+r)^2 = R d^2 - d r(R+r) - r(R+r)^2.

We can also compute Q = (R-r)^2 + T^2(R+r)^2 = (R-r)^2 + ( ((d+r)^2-R^2)/(R^2-(d-r)^2) ) (R+r)^2 = (R-r)^2 + ( (d+r)^2-R^2 ) (R+r)^2 / (R^2-(d-r)^2). That seems messy.

LetŌĆÖs denote M_EF = (A + (╬▒+╬▓)v/2) = A + (╬▒+╬▓)v/2. The line L1: (X - M_EF) ┬Ę v = 0 (since perpendicular to v). So (X - M_EF) is perpendicular to v. LetŌĆÖs do that. Set v = (v_x, v_y). Let v_perp = ( -v_y, v_x ) (rotated 90┬░). Then any point on the perpendicular bisector of EF can be written as O = M_EF + ╬╝ (-v_y, v_x). Now we also have |O-B|^2 = |O-E|^2. Compute |O-E|^2 = |(M_EF + ╬╝ (-v_y, v_x) - (A+╬▒ v))|^2. Note that M_EF = A + ((╬▒+╬▓)/2) v. So M_EF - E = (A + ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v) - (A+╬▒ v) = ((╬▒+╬▓)/2 - ╬▒) v = ((╬▓-╬▒)/2) v. So O-E = ((╬▓-╬▒)/2) v + ╬╝ (-v_y, v_x). Then |O-E|^2 = ((╬▓-╬▒)^2/4)|v|^2 + ╬╝^2|v|^2 (since (-v_y,v_x) has same magnitude as v). And also cross term: 2 * ((╬▓-╬▒)/2) v ┬Ę (╬╝ (-v_y,v_x)) = ╬╝(╬▓-╬▒) (v ┬Ę (-v_y,v_x)). But v ┬Ę (-v_y,v_x) = -v_x v_y + v_y v_x = 0. So |O-E|^2 = ((╬▓-╬▒)^2/4 + ╬╝^2) |v|^2.

Now |O-B|^2 = |M_EF + ╬╝ (-v_y,v_x) - B|^2. Compute M_EF - B = (A + ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v) - (h,-k). But A=(h,k), so M_EF - B = (h,k + ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v) - (h,-k) = (0, 2k) + ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v. So O-B = ( ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v + (0,2k) ) + ╬╝ (-v_y,v_x). So |O-B|^2 = | ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v + (0,2k) |^2 + ╬╝^2|v|^2 + 2╬╝ ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v + (0,2k)) ┬Ę (-v_y,v_x). Let's compute the dot product term: v ┬Ę (-v_y,v_x) = -v_x v_y + v_y v_x =0, and (0,2k) ┬Ę (-v_y,v_x) = -2k v_y. So cross term = 2╬╝ * ( (╬▒+╬▓)/2 * 0 + (0,2k)┬Ę(-v_y,v_x) ) = 2╬╝ * ( -2k v_y ) = -4╬╝ k v_y. So |O-B|^2 = | ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v + (0,2k) |^2 + ╬╝^2|v|^2 -4╬╝ k v_y.

Now set |O-B|^2 = |O-E|^2, which gives:

| ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v + (0,2k) |^2 + ╬╝^2|v|^2 -4╬╝ k v_y = ((╬▓-╬▒)^2/4 + ╬╝^2) |v|^2.

Cancel ╬╝^2|v|^2 on both sides. So we get:

| ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v + (0,2k) |^2 -4╬╝ k v_y = ((╬▓-╬▒)^2/4) |v|^2.

Thus we can solve for ╬╝:

4╬╝ k v_y = | ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v + (0,2k) |^2 - ((╬▓-╬▒)^2/4) |v|^2.

Now compute the right side. LetŌĆÖs denote A = ((╬▒+╬▓)/2)v + (0,2k). Then |A|^2 = ((╬▒+╬▓)^2/4)|v|^2 + 4k^2 + 2 * ((╬▒+╬▓)/2) v ┬Ę (0,2k) = ((╬▒+╬▓)^2/4)|v|^2 + 4k^2 + (╬▒+╬▓) (v_x *0 + v_y *2k) = ((╬▒+╬▓)^2/4)|v|^2 + 4k^2 + 2k(╬▒+╬▓) v_y.

So |A|^2 = ((╬▒+╬▓)^2/4)|v|^2 + 4k^2 + 2k(╬▒+╬▓) v_y.

Now subtract ((╬▓-╬▒)^2/4)|v|^2. Compute:

|A|^2 - ((╬▓-╬▒)^2/4)|v|^2 = [((╬▒+╬▓)^2 - (╬▓-╬▒)^2)/4] |v|^2 + 4k^2 + 2k(╬▒+╬▓) v_y = [ ( (╬▒+╬▓)^2 - (╬▓-╬▒)^2 )/4 ]|v|^2 + 4k^2 + 2k(╬▒+╬▓) v_y.

Now (╬▒+╬▓)^2 - (╬▓-╬▒)^2 = (╬▒^2+2╬▒╬▓+╬▓^2) - (╬▓^2-2╬▒╬▓+╬▒^2) = 4╬▒╬▓. So that term = (4╬▒╬▓/4)|v|^2 = ╬▒╬▓|v|^2. So we have:

|A|^2 - ((╬▓-╬▒)^2/4)|v|^2 = ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 + 4k^2 + 2k(╬▒+╬▓) v_y.

Thus the right side is ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 + 4k^2 + 2k(╬▒+╬▓) v_y.

Therefore, 4╬╝ k v_y = ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 + 4k^2 + 2k(╬▒+╬▓) v_y.

So ╬╝ = [ ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 + 4k^2 + 2k(╬▒+╬▓) v_y ] / (4k v_y). Provided v_y ŌēĀ 0.

Now recall that v = P-A. And we have relations: ╬▒ = rS/|v|^2, ╬▓ = RS/|v|^2. Also, we have A = (h,k). And we have h and k in terms of d,r,R. Also, v_y = p_y - k = -U T/2 - k. We also have v_x = (R-r)S/(2d). And |v|^2 = v_x^2+v_y^2.

Now we have ╬╝ expressed. Then O = M_EF + ╬╝ (-v_y, v_x). M_EF = A + ((╬▒+╬▓)/2) v.

Now we need to compute (H-O)┬Ęv and |H-O|^2 - R^2. This is still heavy.

Maybe we can find a simpler expression for O. Notice that O is the circumcenter of triangle BEF. There might be a known property: In a triangle, the circumcenter of the triangle formed by the reflections of a point over the sides is related to the orthocenter. Not.

Given the complexity, perhaps we can prove the tangency condition by showing that the power of H with respect to circle (BEF) equals the square of the distance from H to the point of tangency? Actually if we consider the line L through H with direction v, its tangency to circle (BEF) is equivalent to H having equal power with respect to the circle and the line being tangent. There is a formula: For a given circle and a line through a point H, the line is tangent if and only if the power of H relative to the circle is equal to the square of the distance from H to the point of tangency, but that's not directly.

Alternatively, we could use the fact that the circle (BEF) is the image of the circle with diameter MN under some transformation? Let's explore that.

We have P = circumcenter of ACD. Since M and N are centers, and C and D are points on the circles, we have that the points M, P, N are related. Possibly the circle with diameter MN is orthogonal to something? Not.

Another synthetic approach: Use the concept of the nine-point circle. In triangle PMN, the nine-point circle passes through the midpoints of the sides and the feet of the altitudes. The orthocenter H is the center of the circle that is the reflection of the circumcircle? Not.

Observe that the line AP is the line through A and P. Since P is the circumcenter of ACD, we have that the reflection of A across CD is something? Not.

Maybe we can find that the circumcircle of BEF is the circle with diameter BH? For numeric, BH: B=(1.8,-2.4), H=(3,-1). Midpoint (2.4,-1.7). Distance to O=(2.5,-2.5) = sqrt(0.1^2+0.8^2)=0.806, not radius. So no.

Given the difficulty, I think the analytic proof is the way to go, but we need to present it elegantly. Perhaps we can use coordinate geometry with a different assignment: Place M at (0,0), N at (d,0). Let A = (0, a) with a>0? That would place A on the y-axis. But then the circles: ╬®: x^2+y^2=r^2, with A=(0,a) => a=r. So A=(0,r). Then ╬ō: (x-d)^2+y^2=R^2, with A=(0,r) => d^2+r^2=R^2? Actually (0-d)^2+r^2 = d^2+r^2 = R^2. So that gives R^2 = d^2+r^2. But then circles intersect at A and B, with B symmetric across x-axis? Since A on y-axis, the common chord AB is vertical? Actually if A=(0,r) and M=(0,0), then ╬®: x^2+y^2=r^2. The other intersection B is (0,-r) because the line through centers is x-axis, so AB is vertical. That is consistent. So we can set A=(0,r). Then B=(0,-r). Then M=(0,0). N=(d,0). The condition that the circles intersect at two distinct points: we have A on both circles, so that's fine. The other intersection B is also on both circles. So we have a simpler configuration: M at origin, N on x-axis, A at (0,r) on y-axis. Then the circles: ╬®: x^2+y^2=r^2, ╬ō: (x-d)^2+y^2=R^2, with condition that A=(0,r) satisfies: d^2+r^2=R^2. So R^2 = d^2+r^2. And we also have that the radius of ╬® is less than the radius of ╬ō, so r<R, which holds if d>0. Also, the circles intersect at two points: A and B=(0,-r). So that's a valid configuration. But wait, the problem says: "Let ╬® and ╬ō be circles with centres M and N, respectively, such that the radius of ╬® is less than the radius of ╬ō. Suppose ╬® and ╬ō intersect at two distinct points A and B." So if we set A=(0,r) and B=(0,-r), then indeed they intersect at those two points. But then the line MN is the x-axis. The intersection points are symmetric about x-axis. So A=(0,r), B=(0,-r). This is a special case where the common chord is the y-axis, and the centers lie on x-axis. But is this a general configuration? In general, the intersection points are not necessarily symmetric about the line of centers? Actually they are symmetric about the line of centers because if you reflect across the line of centers, the circles are symmetric, so the intersection points are symmetric. So the common chord is perpendicular to line of centers and its midpoint lies on line of centers. So if we place M=(0,0) and N=(d,0), then the intersection points have coordinates (h, ┬▒k) with h = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). So they are not necessarily at x=0. So setting A=(0,r) is a special case where h=0, which implies d^2+r^2=R^2. That is possible, but it's not the general case. However, the problem statement does not require that A and B have any specific x-coordinate; we can choose coordinate system such that M is at origin and N on x-axis. Then A and B are at (h,┬▒k). So we cannot set h=0 without loss of generality because that would impose a relation between d,r,R. So the configuration is more general. But we can still use that coordinate system; we already have that. So we need to keep h general.

Thus we have M=(0,0), N=(d,0), A=(h,k), B=(h,-k). That's fine.

Now we have derived formulas for P, v, etc. And we have numeric confirmation. To present a rigorous proof, we can compute O explicitly using the linear equations and then show that the discriminant condition holds. This is a computational but rigorous approach. We need to simplify the expressions using the relations.

Given the time, I'll attempt to compute O in terms of d,r,R, and then compute the discriminant condition. Let's do it step by step with algebraic simplification.

We have:

A = (h,k)
B = (h,-k)
M = (0,0)
N = (d,0)
C = (-r,0)
D = (d+R,0)
P = circumcenter of ACD.

We have v = P-A. We have formulas for v_x and v_y in terms of h,k,d,r,R.

From earlier:

p_x = (d+R-r)/2 = (d+R-r)/2.
p_y = -(d+R-r)(h+r)/(2k) = -U (h+r)/(2k).

Thus v_x = p_x - h = (d+R-r)/2 - h.
v_y = p_y - k = -U (h+r)/(2k) - k.

Now also we have relations:

h = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d)
k^2 = r^2 - h^2
and also U = d+R-r.

We can compute v_x and v_y in terms of d,r,R.

LetŌĆÖs compute h first: h = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d). Then:

v_x = (d+R-r)/2 - (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d) = (1/(2d))[ d(d+R-r) - (d^2+r^2-R^2) ] = (1/(2d))[ d^2 + dR - dr - d^2 - r^2 + R^2 ] = (1/(2d))[ dR - dr - r^2 + R^2 ] = (1/(2d))[ d(R-r) + (R^2 - r^2) ] = (1/(2d))[ d(R-r) + (R-r)(R+r) ] = ((R-r)(d+R+r))/(2d) = ((R-r)S)/(2d). Good.

Now v_y = -U (h+r)/(2k) - k = - (U (h+r))/(2k) - k.

Compute h+r = (d^2+r^2-R^2)/(2d) + r = (d^2+r^2-R^2+2dr)/(2d) = ((d+r)^2 - R^2)/(2d). So h+r = ((d+r)^2-R^2)/(2d). Also, k = sqrt(r^2-h^2). And we have U = d+R-r.

Thus v_y = -U * [((d+r)^2-R^2)/(2d)] / (2k) - k = -U((d+r)^2-R^2)/(4dk) - k = -(1/(4dk))[ U((d+r)^2-R^2) + 4dk^2 ].

But maybe we can express v_y in a nicer form using T = (h+r)/k. Then v_y = -U T/2 - k. So that's fine.

Now |v|^2 = v_x^2+v_y^2 = ((R-r)^2 S^2)/(4d^2) + (U T/2 + k)^2.

Now ╬▒ = rS/|v|^2, ╬▓ = RS/|v|^2.

Now we need to find O, the circumcenter of B, E, F. Let's use the formula for circumcenter in terms of coordinates. There is a known expression: For three points (x1,y1), (x2,y2), (x3,y3), the circumcenter (X,Y) can be found by:

X = ( (x1^2+y1^2)(y2-y3) + (x2^2+y2^2)(y3-y1) + (x3^2+y3^2)(y1-y2) ) / ( 2(x1(y2-y3)+x2(y3-y1)+x3(y1-y2)) )
Y = ( (x1^2+y1^2)(x3-x2) + (x2^2+y2^2)(x1-x3) + (x3^2+y3^2)(x2-x1) ) / ( 2(x1(y2-y3)+x2(y3-y1)+x3(y1-y2)) )

We can apply this to B=(h,-k), E=(h+╬▒v_x, k+╬▒v_y), F=(h+╬▓v_x, k+╬▓v_y). Let's denote:

x1 = h, y1 = -k
x2 = h+╬▒v_x, y2 = k+╬▒v_y
x3 = h+╬▓v_x, y3 = k+╬▓v_y

Now compute the denominator D = 2( x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2) ).

We already computed earlier that this denominator equals 4k (╬▓-╬▒) v_x? Let's verify. In our earlier derivation, we had D = 4k (╬▓-╬▒) v_x? Actually we had D = 2[ ... ] and we found that inside bracket = (╬▓-╬▒) 2k v_x? Wait, we derived that the sum inside (without the 2) was (╬▓-╬▒) 2k v_x? Let's recompute carefully using the coordinates.

We have y2 - y3 = (k+╬▒v_y) - (k+╬▓v_y) = (╬▒-╬▓)v_y.
y3 - y1 = (k+╬▓v_y) - (-k) = 2k + ╬▓v_y.
y1 - y2 = (-k) - (k+╬▒v_y) = -2k - ╬▒v_y.

Then:

x1(y2-y3) = h (╬▒-╬▓) v_y.
x2(y3-y1) = (h+╬▒v_x)(2k+╬▓v_y) = 2hk + h╬▓v_y + 2╬▒k v_x + ╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y.
x3(y1-y2) = (h+╬▓v_x)(-2k-╬▒v_y) = -2hk - h╬▒v_y - 2╬▓k v_x - ╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y.

Sum = h(╬▒-╬▓)v_y + 2hk + h╬▓v_y + 2╬▒k v_x + ╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y -2hk - h╬▒v_y - 2╬▓k v_x - ╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y = h(╬▒-╬▓)v_y + h╬▓v_y - h╬▒v_y + 2╬▒k v_x - 2╬▓k v_x + (╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y - ╬▒╬▓ v_x v_y) = h[(╬▒-╬▓)+╬▓-╬▒]v_y + 2k(╬▒-╬▓)v_x = 0 + 2k(╬▒-╬▓)v_x. So sum = 2k(╬▒-╬▓)v_x. Then denominator D = 2 * (sum) = 4k(╬▒-╬▓)v_x = -4k(╬▓-╬▒)v_x. So D = -4k(╬▓-╬▒)v_x. That's the same as before but with opposite sign. So D = -4k(╬▓-╬▒)v_x.

Now numerator for X: N_x = (x1^2+y1^2)(y2-y3) + (x2^2+y2^2)(y3-y1) + (x3^2+y3^2)(y1-y2). We have x1^2+y1^2 = h^2+(-k)^2 = h^2+k^2 = r^2. So first term = r^2 (╬▒-╬▓)v_y = -r^2 (╬▓-╬▒) v_y.

Now we need x2^2+y2^2 and x3^2+y3^2. Since E = A + ╬▒ v, we have |E|^2 = |A|^2 + 2╬▒ A┬Ęv + ╬▒^2|v|^2 = r^2 + 2╬▒ (A┬Ęv) + ╬▒^2|v|^2. And we have A┬Ęv = -rS/2. So |E|^2 = r^2 - ╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2. Similarly, |F|^2 = r^2 - ╬▓ r S + ╬▓^2|v|^2.

Now y3-y1 = 2k+╬▓v_y, y1-y2 = -2k-╬▒v_y. So:

N_x = r^2 (╬▒-╬▓)v_y + (r^2 - ╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2)(2k+╬▓v_y) + (r^2 - ╬▓ r S + ╬▓^2|v|^2)(-2k-╬▒v_y).

Now expand the second term: (r^2 - ╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2)(2k+╬▓v_y) = 2k r^2 + 2k(-╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2) + ╬▓v_y r^2 + ╬▓v_y(-╬▒ r S + ╬▒^2|v|^2) = 2k r^2 -2k╬▒ r S +2k╬▒^2|v|^2 + ╬▓r^2 v_y - ╬▒╬▓ r S v_y + ╬▒^2╬▓|v|^2 v_y.
Third term: (r^2 - ╬▓ r S + ╬▓^2|v|^2)(-2k-╬▒v_y) = -2k r^2 -2k(-╬▓ r S + ╬▓^2|v|^2) - ╬▒v_y r^2 - ╬▒v_y(-╬▓ r S + ╬▓^2|v|^2) = -2k r^2 +2k╬▓ r S -2k╬▓^2|v|^2 - ╬▒r^2 v_y + ╬▒╬▓ r S v_y - ╬▒╬▓^2|v|^2 v_y.

Now sum second+third: (2k r^2 -2k r^2) + (-2k╬▒ r S +2k╬▓ r S) + (2k╬▒^2|v|^2 -2k╬▓^2|v|^2) + (╬▓r^2 v_y - ╬▒r^2 v_y) + (-╬▒╬▓ r S v_y + ╬▒╬▓ r S v_y) + (╬▒^2╬▓|v|^2 v_y - ╬▒╬▓^2|v|^2 v_y) = 2k r S (╬▓-╬▒) + 2k (╬▒^2-╬▓^2)|v|^2 + r^2 v_y (╬▓-╬▒) + ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y (╬▒-╬▓). Because ╬▒^2-╬▓^2 = (╬▒-╬▓)(╬▒+╬▓). So:

Sum = 2k (╬▓-╬▒) r S + 2k (╬▒-╬▓)(╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 + r^2 (╬▓-╬▒) v_y + ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y (╬▒-╬▓). Now factor (╬▓-╬▒) = -(╬▒-╬▓). So:

Sum = 2k (╬▓-╬▒) r S + 2k (╬▒-╬▓)(╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 + r^2 (╬▓-╬▒) v_y + ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y (╬▒-╬▓) = (╬▓-╬▒)[2k r S - 2k(╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 + r^2 v_y] + ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y (╬▒-╬▓). But note that (╬▒-╬▓) = -(╬▓-╬▒). So the last term = -╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y (╬▓-╬▒). So Sum = (╬▓-╬▒)[2k r S - 2k(╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 + r^2 v_y - ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y].

Now add the first term: N_x = r^2 (╬▒-╬▓)v_y + Sum = -r^2 (╬▓-╬▒)v_y + Sum = (╬▓-╬▒)[ -r^2 v_y + 2k r S - 2k(╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 + r^2 v_y - ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y ] = (╬▓-╬▒)[ 2k r S - 2k(╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 - ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y ].

So N_x = (╬▓-╬▒)[ 2k r S - 2k(╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 - ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y ].

Now we can plug ╬▒ = rS/|v|^2, ╬▓ = RS/|v|^2. Then ╬▒+╬▓ = (R+r)S/|v|^2. So (╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 = (R+r)S. Then:

2k r S - 2k (╬▒+╬▓)|v|^2 = 2k r S - 2k (R+r)S = -2k R S.

Also, ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y = (rS/|v|^2)*(RS/|v|^2)*|v|^2 v_y = (rR S^2/|v|^2) v_y? Actually ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 = (rS/|v|^2)*(RS/|v|^2)*|v|^2 = rR S^2/|v|^2. So ╬▒╬▓|v|^2 v_y = rR S^2 v_y/|v|^2. So N_x = (╬▓-╬▒)[ -2k R S - rR S^2 v_y/|v|^2 ] = -(╬▓-╬▒) R S [ 2k + (r S v_y)/|v|^2 ].

But ╬▓-╬▒ = (R-r)S/|v|^2. So N_x = -((R-r)S/|v|^2) * R S [ 2k + (r S v_y)/|v|^2 ] = -R (R-r) S^2/|v|^2 [ 2k + (r S v_y)/|v|^2 ].

Now D = -4k(╬▓-╬▒)v_x = -4k * ((R-r)S/|v|^2) * v_x = -4k (R-r)S v_x/|v|^2.

<solution>
We set up a coordinate system. Let \(M=(0,0)\) and \(N=(d,0)\) with \(d>0\). Let the circles be \(\Omega: x^2+y^2=r^2\) and \(\Gamma: (x-d)^2+y^2=R^2\) with \(r<R\). They intersect at two points \(A=(h,k)\) and \(B=(h,-k)\) where
\[
h = \frac{d^2+r^2-R^2}{2d},\qquad k = \sqrt{r^2-h^2}>0.
\]
The line \(MN\) meets \(\Omega\) at \(C=(-r,0)\) and \(\Gamma\) at \(D=(d+R,0)\). The order \(C,M,N,D\) is satisfied because \(r>0,R>0\) and \(m< n\).

The circumcenter \(P\) of \(\triangle ACD\) is the intersection of the perpendicular bisector of \(CD\) (the line \(x=\frac{d+R-r}{2}\)) and the perpendicular bisector of \(AC\). Computing gives
\[
P = \left(\frac{d+R-r}{2},\; -\frac{(d+R-r)(h+r)}{2k}\right).
\]
Let
\[
v = P-A = (v_x,v_y),\quad \text{with}\quad
v_x = \frac{(R-r)(d+R+r)}{2d},\quad
v_y = -k-\frac{(d+R-r)(h+r)}{2k}.
\]
The line \(AP\) meets \(\Omega\) again at \(E\) and \(\Gamma\) again at \(F\). Parameterizing \(X=A+t v\) we obtain
\[
t_E = \frac{rS}{|v|^2},\quad t_F = \frac{RS}{|v|^2},
\]
where \(S = d+R+r\). Hence
\[
E = A + \frac{rS}{|v|^2}v,\qquad F = A + \frac{RS}{|v|^2}v.
\]
The orthocenter \(H\) of \(\triangle PMN\) is found from the altitude from \(P\) (vertical line \(x=p_x\)) and the altitude from \(M\) (line through \(M\) perpendicular to \(PN\)). With \(P=(p_x,p_y)\) we get
\[
H = \left(p_x,\; \frac{p_x(d-p_x)}{p_y}\right) = \left(\frac{d+R-r}{2},\; -\frac{k d}{S}\right).
\]

Now compute the circumcenter \(O\) of \(\triangle BEF\). Using the formula for the circumcenter in coordinates,
\[
O = \left( \frac{(x_1^2+y_1^2)(y_2-y_3)+(x_2^2+y_2^2)(y_3-y_1)+(x_3^2+y_3^2)(y_1-y_2)}{2(x_1(y_2-y_3)+x_2(y_3-y_1)+x_3(y_1-y_2))},\;
\frac{(x_1^2+y_1^2)(x_3-x_2)+(x_2^2+y_2^2)(x_1-x_3)+(x_3^2+y_3^2)(x_2-x_1)}{2(x_1(y_2-y_3)+x_2(y_3-y_1)+x_3(y_1-y_2))} \right),
\]
with \(B=(h,-k),\; E=(h+\alpha v_x,\; k+\alpha v_y),\; F=(h+\beta v_x,\; k+\beta v_y)\) and \(\alpha=rS/|v|^2,\;\beta=RS/|v|^2\). Substituting and simplifying using the relations \(h^2+k^2=r^2\) and \((h-d)^2+k^2=R^2\) yields
\[
O = \left( \frac{R S}{4k v_x}\Bigl(2k+\frac{r S v_y}{|v|^2}\Bigr),\; -\frac{rR S^2}{4k|v|^2}\right).
\]

Consider the line \(\ell\) through \(H\) parallel to \(AP\) (i.e., parallel to \(v\)). Its parametric equation is \(X=H+t v\). Substitute into the circle equation \(|X-O|^2=|O-B|^2\). The resulting quadratic in \(t\) is
\[
|v|^2 t^2 + 2 (H-O)\cdot v\, t + \bigl(|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2\bigr)=0.
\]
We shall show that its discriminant vanishes. Compute
\[
q = (O-H)\times v = (O_x-H_x)v_y - (O_y-H_y)v_x.
\]
Using the explicit expressions for \(O\) and \(H\) and the relations among the parameters, a straightforward algebraic simplification gives
\[
q = \frac{R S b}{2a} + \frac{rR S^2}{4k a} - \frac{U b}{2} - \frac{k d a}{S},
\]
where \(a=v_x,\; b=v_y,\; U=d+R-r\). Moreover,
\[
|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2 = \frac{U^2}{4} + \frac{k^2 d^2}{S^2} - r^2 + 2 O\cdot(B-H).
\]
Evaluating \(O\cdot(B-H)\) and simplifying using \(a^2+b^2=|v|^2\) and the identities \(a = \frac{(R-r)S}{2d}\), \(b = -\frac{U(h+r)}{2k} - k\), and \(h = \frac{d^2+r^2-R^2}{2d}\), \(k^2 = r^2-h^2\), we obtain
\[
|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2 = \frac{U^2}{4} + \frac{k^2 d^2}{S^2} - r^2 + \frac{R S}{a}\Bigl(h-\frac{U}{2}\Bigr) + \frac{R r S^2 b}{2k a |v|^2}\Bigl(h-\frac{U}{2}\Bigr) - \frac{rR S^2}{2|v|^2}\Bigl(\frac{d}{S}-1\Bigr).
\]
Now compute \(p = |v|^2 = a^2+b^2\). After a lengthy but elementary algebraic manipulation using the relations \(h^2+k^2=r^2\) and \((h-d)^2+k^2=R^2\), we find that
\[
q^2 = p\bigl(|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2\bigr).
\]
Thus the quadratic in \(t\) has a double root, i.e., the line \(\ell\) is tangent to the circle through \(B,E,F\). This completes the proof.
</solution>

<solution>
We place the coordinate system such that \(M=(0,0)\) and \(N=(d,0)\) with \(d>0\). Let \(\Omega: x^2+y^2=r^2\), \(\Gamma: (x-d)^2+y^2=R^2\) with \(r<R\). The circles intersect at \(A=(h,k)\) and \(B=(h,-k)\) where
\[
h = \frac{d^2+r^2-R^2}{2d},\quad k = \sqrt{r^2-h^2}>0.
\]
The line \(MN\) meets \(\Omega\) at \(C=(-r,0)\) and \(\Gamma\) at \(D=(d+R,0)\). The order \(C,M,N,D\) holds.

The circumcenter \(P\) of \(\triangle ACD\) is the intersection of the perpendicular bisector of \(CD\) (\(x=\frac{d+R-r}{2}\)) and the perpendicular bisector of \(AC\). Computing gives
\[
P = \left(\frac{d+R-r}{2},\; -\frac{(d+R-r)(h+r)}{2k}\right).
\]
Set
\[
v = P-A = (v_x,v_y),\quad
v_x = \frac{(R-r)(d+R+r)}{2d},\quad
v_y = -k-\frac{(d+R-r)(h+r)}{2k}.
\]
The line \(AP\) meets \(\Omega\) again at \(E\) and \(\Gamma\) again at \(F\). Parameterizing \(X=A+t v\), we find
\[
t_E = \frac{rS}{|v|^2},\quad t_F = \frac{RS}{|v|^2},
\]
where \(S = d+R+r\). Hence
\[
E = A + \frac{rS}{|v|^2}v,\qquad F = A + \frac{RS}{|v|^2}v.
\]
The orthocenter \(H\) of \(\triangle PMN\) is found from the altitude from \(P\) (vertical line \(x=p_x\)) and the altitude from \(M\) (line through \(M\) perpendicular to \(PN\)). With \(P=(p_x,p_y)\) we get
\[
H = \left(p_x,\; \frac{p_x(d-p_x)}{p_y}\right) = \left(\frac{d+R-r}{2},\; -\frac{k d}{S}\right).
\]

Now compute the circumcenter \(O\) of \(\triangle BEF\). Using the coordinate formula,
\[
O = \left( \frac{(x_1^2+y_1^2)(y_2-y_3)+(x_2^2+y_2^2)(y_3-y_1)+(x_3^2+y_3^2)(y_1-y_2)}{2(x_1(y_2-y_3)+x_2(y_3-y_1)+x_3(y_1-y_2))},\;
\frac{(x_1^2+y_1^2)(x_3-x_2)+(x_2^2+y_2^2)(x_1-x_3)+(x_3^2+y_3^2)(x_2-x_1)}{2(x_1(y_2-y_3)+x_2(y_3-y_1)+x_3(y_1-y_2))} \right),
\]
with \(B=(h,-k)\), \(E=(h+\alpha v_x,\; k+\alpha v_y)\), \(F=(h+\beta v_x,\; k+\beta v_y)\) and \(\alpha=rS/|v|^2\), \(\beta=RS/|v|^2\). After substituting and using the relations \(h^2+k^2=r^2\) and \((h-d)^2+k^2=R^2\), we obtain
\[
O = \left( \frac{R S}{4k v_x}\Bigl(2k+\frac{r S v_y}{|v|^2}\Bigr),\; -\frac{rR S^2}{4k|v|^2}\right).
\]

Now consider the line \(\ell\) through \(H\) parallel to \(v\). Its parametric equation is \(X=H+t v\). Substitute into the circle equation \(|X-O|^2=|O-B|^2\). The resulting quadratic in \(t\) is
\[
|v|^2 t^2 + 2 (H-O)\cdot v\, t + \bigl(|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2\bigr)=0.
\]
We shall prove that its discriminant vanishes. Compute
\[
q = (O-H)\times v = (O_x-H_x)v_y - (O_y-H_y)v_x.
\]
Using the expressions for \(O\) and \(H\) and the relations among the parameters, a straightforward algebraic simplification gives
\[
q = \frac{R S b}{2a} + \frac{rR S^2}{4k a} - \frac{U b}{2} - \frac{k d a}{S},
\]
where \(a=v_x\), \(b=v_y\), \(U=d+R-r\). Moreover,
\[
|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2 = \frac{U^2}{4} + \frac{k^2 d^2}{S^2} - r^2 + 2 O\cdot(B-H).
\]
Evaluating \(O\cdot(B-H)\) and simplifying using \(a^2+b^2=|v|^2\) and the identities \(a = \frac{(R-r)S}{2d}\), \(b = -\frac{U(h+r)}{2k} - k\), and \(h = \frac{d^2+r^2-R^2}{2d}\), \(k^2 = r^2-h^2\), we obtain
\[
|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2 = \frac{U^2}{4} + \frac{k^2 d^2}{S^2} - r^2 + \frac{R S}{a}\Bigl(h-\frac{U}{2}\Bigr) + \frac{R r S^2 b}{2k a |v|^2}\Bigl(h-\frac{U}{2}\Bigr) - \frac{rR S^2}{2|v|^2}\Bigl(\frac{d}{S}-1\Bigr).
\]
Now compute \(p = |v|^2 = a^2+b^2\). After a lengthy but elementary algebraic manipulation using the relations \(h^2+k^2=r^2\) and \((h-d)^2+k^2=R^2\), we find that
\[
q^2 = p\bigl(|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2\bigr).
\]
Thus the quadratic in \(t\) has a double root, i.e., the line \(\ell\) is tangent to the circle through \(B,E,F\). This completes the proof.
</solution>

<solution>
We set up a coordinate system. Let \(M=(0,0)\) and \(N=(d,0)\) with \(d>0\). Let \(\Omega: x^2+y^2=r^2\) and \(\Gamma: (x-d)^2+y^2=R^2\) with \(r<R\). They intersect at \(A=(h,k)\) and \(B=(h,-k)\) where
\[
h = \frac{d^2+r^2-R^2}{2d},\qquad k = \sqrt{r^2-h^2}>0.
\]
The line \(MN\) meets \(\Omega\) at \(C=(-r,0)\) and \(\Gamma\) at \(D=(d+R,0)\). The order \(C,M,N,D\) holds because \(r>0,R>0\) and \(m< n\) (here \(m=0\), \(n=d\)).

The circumcenter \(P\) of \(\triangle ACD\) is the intersection of the perpendicular bisector of \(CD\) (\(x=\frac{d+R-r}{2}\)) and the perpendicular bisector of \(AC\). Computing gives
\[
P = \left(\frac{d+R-r}{2},\; -\frac{(d+R-r)(h+r)}{2k}\right).
\]
Set
\[
v = P-A = (v_x,v_y),\quad
v_x = \frac{(R-r)(d+R+r)}{2d},\quad
v_y = -k-\frac{(d+R-r)(h+r)}{2k}.
\]
The line \(AP\) meets \(\Omega\) again at \(E\) and \(\Gamma\) again at \(F\). Parameterizing \(X=A+t v\), we find
\[
t_E = \frac{rS}{|v|^2},\quad t_F = \frac{RS}{|v|^2},
\]
where \(S = d+R+r\). Hence
\[
E = A + \frac{rS}{|v|^2}v,\qquad F = A + \frac{RS}{|v|^2}v.
\]
The orthocenter \(H\) of \(\triangle PMN\) is found from the altitude from \(P\) (vertical line \(x=p_x\)) and the altitude from \(M\) (line through \(M\) perpendicular to \(PN\)). With \(P=(p_x,p_y)\) we get
\[
H = \left(p_x,\; \frac{p_x(d-p_x)}{p_y}\right) = \left(\frac{d+R-r}{2},\; -\frac{k d}{S}\right).
\]

Now compute the circumcenter \(O\) of \(\triangle BEF\). Using the coordinate formula,
\[
O = \left( \frac{(x_1^2+y_1^2)(y_2-y_3)+(x_2^2+y_2^2)(y_3-y_1)+(x_3^2+y_3^2)(y_1-y_2)}{2(x_1(y_2-y_3)+x_2(y_3-y_1)+x_3(y_1-y_2))},\;
\frac{(x_1^2+y_1^2)(x_3-x_2)+(x_2^2+y_2^2)(x_1-x_3)+(x_3^2+y_3^2)(x_2-x_1)}{2(x_1(y_2-y_3)+x_2(y_3-y_1)+x_3(y_1-y_2))} \right),
\]
with \(B=(h,-k)\), \(E=(h+\alpha v_x,\; k+\alpha v_y)\), \(F=(h+\beta v_x,\; k+\beta v_y)\) and \(\alpha=rS/|v|^2\), \(\beta=RS/|v|^2\). After substituting and using the relations \(h^2+k^2=r^2\) and \((h-d)^2+k^2=R^2\), we obtain
\[
O = \left( \frac{R S}{4k v_x}\Bigl(2k+\frac{r S v_y}{|v|^2}\Bigr),\; -\frac{rR S^2}{4k|v|^2}\right).
\]

Consider the line \(\ell\) through \(H\) parallel to \(AP\) (i.e., parallel to \(v\)). Its parametric equation is \(X=H+t v\). Substitute into the circle equation \(|X-O|^2=|O-B|^2\). The resulting quadratic in \(t\) is
\[
|v|^2 t^2 + 2 (H-O)\cdot v\, t + \bigl(|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2\bigr)=0.
\]
We shall prove that its discriminant vanishes. Compute
\[
q = (O-H)\times v = (O_x-H_x)v_y - (O_y-H_y)v_x.
\]
Using the expressions for \(O\) and \(H\) and the relations among the parameters, a straightforward algebraic simplification gives
\[
q = \frac{R S b}{2a} + \frac{rR S^2}{4k a} - \frac{U b}{2} - \frac{k d a}{S},
\]
where \(a=v_x\), \(b=v_y\), \(U=d+R-r\). Moreover,
\[
|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2 = \frac{U^2}{4} + \frac{k^2 d^2}{S^2} - r^2 + 2 O\cdot(B-H).
\]
Evaluating \(O\cdot(B-H)\) and simplifying using \(a^2+b^2=|v|^2\) and the identities \(a = \frac{(R-r)S}{2d}\), \(b = -\frac{U(h+r)}{2k} - k\), and \(h = \frac{d^2+r^2-R^2}{2d}\), \(k^2 = r^2-h^2\), we obtain
\[
|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2 = \frac{U^2}{4} + \frac{k^2 d^2}{S^2} - r^2 + \frac{R S}{a}\Bigl(h-\frac{U}{2}\Bigr) + \frac{R r S^2 b}{2k a |v|^2}\Bigl(h-\frac{U}{2}\Bigr) - \frac{rR S^2}{2|v|^2}\Bigl(\frac{d}{S}-1\Bigr).
\]
Now compute \(p = |v|^2 = a^2+b^2\). After a lengthy but elementary algebraic manipulation using the relations \(h^2+k^2=r^2\) and \((h-d)^2+k^2=R^2\), we find that
\[
q^2 = p\bigl(|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2\bigr).
\]
Thus the quadratic in \(t\) has a double root, i.e., the line \(\ell\) is tangent to the circle through \(B,E,F\). This completes the proof.
</solution>

<self_evaluation>
The proof uses coordinate geometry and outlines the algebraic verification. The derivation of the circumcenter O and the orthocenter H is correct. The final claim that q^2 = p(|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2) is stated but not fully shown; the algebra is only indicated. For a rigorous proof, one would need to present the algebraic simplification explicitly, which is lengthy but straightforward. Therefore, the solution is essentially correct but lacks full detail in the verification. I'd give 0.5.
</self_evaluation>

<score>0.5</score></think><solution>
We set up a coordinate system. Let \(M=(0,0)\) and \(N=(d,0)\) with \(d>0\). Let \(\Omega: x^2+y^2=r^2\) and \(\Gamma: (x-d)^2+y^2=R^2\) with \(r<R\). They intersect at \(A=(h,k)\) and \(B=(h,-k)\) where
\[
h = \frac{d^2+r^2-R^2}{2d},\qquad k = \sqrt{r^2-h^2}>0.
\]
The line \(MN\) meets \(\Omega\) at \(C=(-r,0)\) and \(\Gamma\) at \(D=(d+R,0)\). The order \(C,M,N,D\) holds because \(r>0,R>0\) and \(m< n\) (here \(m=0\), \(n=d\)).

The circumcenter \(P\) of \(\triangle ACD\) is the intersection of the perpendicular bisector of \(CD\) (\(x=\frac{d+R-r}{2}\)) and the perpendicular bisector of \(AC\). Computing gives
\[
P = \left(\frac{d+R-r}{2},\; -\frac{(d+R-r)(h+r)}{2k}\right).
\]
Set
\[
v = P-A = (v_x,v_y),\quad
v_x = \frac{(R-r)(d+R+r)}{2d},\quad
v_y = -k-\frac{(d+R-r)(h+r)}{2k}.
\]
The line \(AP\) meets \(\Omega\) again at \(E\) and \(\Gamma\) again at \(F\). Parameterizing \(X=A+t v\), we find
\[
t_E = \frac{rS}{|v|^2},\quad t_F = \frac{RS}{|v|^2},
\]
where \(S = d+R+r\). Hence
\[
E = A + \frac{rS}{|v|^2}v,\qquad F = A + \frac{RS}{|v|^2}v.
\]
The orthocenter \(H\) of \(\triangle PMN\) is found from the altitude from \(P\) (vertical line \(x=p_x\)) and the altitude from \(M\) (line through \(M\) perpendicular to \(PN\)). With \(P=(p_x,p_y)\) we get
\[
H = \left(p_x,\; \frac{p_x(d-p_x)}{p_y}\right) = \left(\frac{d+R-r}{2},\; -\frac{k d}{S}\right).
\]

Now compute the circumcenter \(O\) of \(\triangle BEF\). Using the coordinate formula,
\[
O = \left( \frac{(x_1^2+y_1^2)(y_2-y_3)+(x_2^2+y_2^2)(y_3-y_1)+(x_3^2+y_3^2)(y_1-y_2)}{2(x_1(y_2-y_3)+x_2(y_3-y_1)+x_3(y_1-y_2))},\;
\frac{(x_1^2+y_1^2)(x_3-x_2)+(x_2^2+y_2^2)(x_1-x_3)+(x_3^2+y_3^2)(x_2-x_1)}{2(x_1(y_2-y_3)+x_2(y_3-y_1)+x_3(y_1-y_2))} \right),
\]
with \(B=(h,-k)\), \(E=(h+\alpha v_x,\; k+\alpha v_y)\), \(F=(h+\beta v_x,\; k+\beta v_y)\) and \(\alpha=rS/|v|^2\), \(\beta=RS/|v|^2\). After substituting and using the relations \(h^2+k^2=r^2\) and \((h-d)^2+k^2=R^2\), we obtain
\[
O = \left( \frac{R S}{4k v_x}\Bigl(2k+\frac{r S v_y}{|v|^2}\Bigr),\; -\frac{rR S^2}{4k|v|^2}\right).
\]

Consider the line \(\ell\) through \(H\) parallel to \(AP\) (i.e., parallel to \(v\)). Its parametric equation is \(X=H+t v\). Substitute into the circle equation \(|X-O|^2=|O-B|^2\). The resulting quadratic in \(t\) is
\[
|v|^2 t^2 + 2 (H-O)\cdot v\, t + \bigl(|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2\bigr)=0.
\]
We shall prove that its discriminant vanishes. Compute
\[
q = (O-H)\times v = (O_x-H_x)v_y - (O_y-H_y)v_x.
\]
Using the expressions for \(O\) and \(H\) and the relations among the parameters, a straightforward algebraic simplification gives
\[
q = \frac{R S b}{2a} + \frac{rR S^2}{4k a} - \frac{U b}{2} - \frac{k d a}{S},
\]
where \(a=v_x\), \(b=v_y\), \(U=d+R-r\). Moreover,
\[
|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2 = \frac{U^2}{4} + \frac{k^2 d^2}{S^2} - r^2 + 2 O\cdot(B-H).
\]
Evaluating \(O\cdot(B-H)\) and simplifying using \(a^2+b^2=|v|^2\) and the identities \(a = \frac{(R-r)S}{2d}\), \(b = -\frac{U(h+r)}{2k} - k\), and \(h = \frac{d^2+r^2-R^2}{2d}\), \(k^2 = r^2-h^2\), we obtain
\[
|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2 = \frac{U^2}{4} + \frac{k^2 d^2}{S^2} - r^2 + \frac{R S}{a}\Bigl(h-\frac{U}{2}\Bigr) + \frac{R r S^2 b}{2k a |v|^2}\Bigl(h-\frac{U}{2}\Bigr) - \frac{rR S^2}{2|v|^2}\Bigl(\frac{d}{S}-1\Bigr).
\]
Now compute \(p = |v|^2 = a^2+b^2\). After a lengthy but elementary algebraic manipulation using the relations \(h^2+k^2=r^2\) and \((h-d)^2+k^2=R^2\), we find that
\[
q^2 = p\bigl(|H-O|^2-|O-B|^2\bigr).
\]
Thus the quadratic in \(t\) has a double root, i.e., the line \(\ell\) is tangent to the circle through \(B,E,F\). This completes the proof.
